     <p><b>Dalhousie University</b> (commonly known as <b>Dalhousie</b> or <b>Dal</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, Canada, with three campuses in <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a>, and a fourth in <a href="/wiki/Bible_Hill,_Nova_Scotia" title="Bible Hill, Nova Scotia">Bible Hill</a>. Dalhousie offers more than 3,700 courses and 190 degree programs in twelve undergraduate, graduate, and professional faculties. The university is a member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a>, a group of research-intensive universities in Canada.</p> 
     <p>Dalhousie was established as a <a href="/wiki/Nonsectarian" title="Nonsectarian">nonsectarian</a> college in 1818 by the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia">Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Ramsay,_9th_Earl_of_Dalhousie" title="George Ramsay, 9th Earl of Dalhousie">George Ramsay, 9th Earl of Dalhousie</a>, after whom the university was named. The college did not hold its first class until 1838, until then operating sporadically due to financial difficulties. It reopened for a third time in 1863 following a reorganization which brought a change of name to &quot;The Governors of Dalhousie College and University&quot;. The university had formally changed its name to &quot;Dalhousie University&quot; in 1997 through provincial legislation, the same legislation which had merged the institution with the <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Technical University of Nova Scotia">Technical University of Nova Scotia</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Dalhousie library system currently operates the largest library in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, as well as holds the largest collection of agricultural resource material in the region. The university operates a total of fourteen residences. There are currently two <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">student unions</a> that represent student interests at the university, the <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Student_Union" title="Dalhousie Student Union">Dalhousie Student Union</a>, and the Dalhousie Association for Graduate Students. Dalhousie's varsity teams, the Tigers, compete in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_University_Sport" title="Atlantic University Sport">Atlantic University Sport</a> conference of <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a>. Dalhousie’s Faculty of Agriculture varsity teams are the Dalhousie Rams, and compete in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="Atlantic Collegiate Athletic Association">ACAA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="Canadian Collegiate Athletic Association">CCAA</a>.</p> 
     <p>Dalhousie is a <a href="/wiki/Mixed-sex_education" title="Mixed-sex education">coeducational</a> university with more than 18,000 students and over 110,000 alumni. Notable alumni include government officials, academics, business leaders and 87 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholars</a>. The university ranked 234th in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-QS_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> 251-275th in the 2012-2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> and 201–300th in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie is a centre for marine research, and is host to the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Tracking_Network" title="Ocean Tracking Network">Ocean Tracking Network</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Original Dalhousie University building circa 1871" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg/220px-Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg/330px-Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg/440px-Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dalhousie_College_Halifax_Canada_1871.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The original Dalhousie College building shown that faced the 
        <a href="/wiki/Grand_Parade_(Halifax)" title="Grand Parade (Halifax)">Grand Parade</a> in downtown Halifax.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width: 20%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;"> 
      <div style="position: relative; text-align: left;"> 
       <div> 
        <p>&quot;[F]ounded on the principles of religious tolerance&quot;.</p> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <div style="text-align: left;">
       — 
       <a href="/wiki/George_Ramsay,_9th_Earl_of_Dalhousie" title="George Ramsay, 9th Earl of Dalhousie">George Ramsay, 9th Earl of Dalhousie</a>, 1820
       <sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Dalhousie was founded as the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia">Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Ramsay,_9th_Earl_of_Dalhousie" title="George Ramsay, 9th Earl of Dalhousie">George Ramsay, 9th Earl of Dalhousie</a> desired a non-denominational college in Halifax. Financing largely came from customs duties collected by a previous Lieutenant Governor, <a href="/wiki/John_Coape_Sherbrooke" title="John Coape Sherbrooke">John Coape Sherbrooke</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> occupation of <a href="/wiki/Castine,_Maine" title="Castine, Maine">Castine, Maine</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>a<span>]</span></a></sup> Sherbrooke invested <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">GBP&pound;</a>7,000 as an initial endowment and reserved &pound;3,000 for the physical construction of the college.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite199710_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite199710-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The college was established in 1818, though it faltered shortly after as Ramsay left Halifax to serve as the <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of British North America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dalhis_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalhis-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The school was structured upon the principles of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a>, where lectures were open to all, regardless of religioun or nationality. The University of Edinburgh was located near Ramsay's home in Scotland.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite199418_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite199418-11"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1821 Dalhousie College was officially incorporated by the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_House_of_Assembly" title="Nova Scotia House of Assembly">Nova Scotia House of Assembly</a> under the 1821 Act of Incorporation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite199723_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite199723-12"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The college did not hold its first class until 1838; operation of the college was intermittent and no degrees were awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-dalhis_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalhis-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1841 an Act of the Nova Scotia House of Assembly conferred university powers on Dalhousie.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurray20103_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurray20103-13"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1863 the college opened for a third time and was reorganized by another legislative act, which added &quot;university&quot; to the school's name: &quot;The Governors of Dalhousie College and University&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite199495_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite199495-14"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dalsta_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalsta-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie reopened with six professors and one tutor. When it awarded its first degrees in 1866 the student body consisted of 28 students working toward degrees and 28 occasional students.<sup id="cite_ref-dalhis_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalhis-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> The first female graduate was Margaret Florence Newcome from <a href="/wiki/Grafton,_Nova_Scotia" title="Grafton, Nova Scotia">Grafton, Nova Scotia</a>, who earned her degree in 1885.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the reorganization and an increase in students, money continued to be a problem for the institution. In 1879, amid talks of closure due to the university's dire financial situation, a wealthy New York publisher with Nova Scotia roots, <a href="/wiki/George_Munro_(philanthropist)" title="George Munro (philanthropist)">George Munro</a>, began to donate to the university; Munro was brother-in-law to Dalhousie's Board of Governors member <a href="/wiki/John_Forrest_(Canadian_clergyman)" title="John Forrest (Canadian clergyman)">John Forrest</a>. Munro is credited with rescuing Dalhousie from closure, and in honour of his contributions Dalhousie observes a university holiday called George Munro Day on the first Friday of each February.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Originally located at the space now occupied by <a href="/wiki/Halifax_City_Hall" title="Halifax City Hall">Halifax City Hall</a>, the college moved in 1886 to Carleton Campus and spread gradually to Studley Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-dalhis_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalhis-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie grew steadily during the 20th century. From 1889 to 1962 the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Conservatory_of_Performing_Arts" title="Maritime Conservatory of Performing Arts">Halifax Conservatory</a> was affiliated with and awarded degrees through the Dalhousie.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1920 several buildings were destroyed by fire on the campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_King%27s_College" title="University of King's College">University of King's College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Nova_Scotia" title="Windsor, Nova Scotia">Windsor, Nova Scotia</a>. Through a grant from the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Corporation_of_New_York" title="Carnegie Corporation of New York">Carnegie Foundation</a>, King's College relocated to Halifax and entered into a partnership with Dalhousie which continues to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Dalhousie expanded on 1 April 1997 when provincial legislation mandated an amalgamation with the nearby <a href="/wiki/Technical_University_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Technical University of Nova Scotia">Technical University of Nova Scotia</a>. This merger saw reorganization of faculties and departments to create the <a href="/wiki/Faculty_of_Engineering,_Dalhousie_University" title="Faculty of Engineering, Dalhousie University">Faculty of Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faculty_of_Computer_Science,_Dalhousie_University" title="Faculty of Computer Science, Dalhousie University">Faculty of Computer Science</a> and the Faculty of Architecture and Planning.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1997 to 2000, the Technical University of Nova Scotia operated as a constituent college of Dalhousie called Dalhousie Polytechnic of Nova Scotia (DalTech) until the collegiate system was dissolved.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The same legislation which merged the two schools also formally changed the name of the institution to its present form, Dalhousie University.<sup id="cite_ref-nslegislature.ca_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nslegislature.ca-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> On 1 September 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Agricultural_College" title="Nova Scotia Agricultural College">Nova Scotia Agricultural College</a> merged into Dalhousie to form a new <a href="/wiki/Faculty_of_Agriculture,_Dalhousie_University" title="Faculty of Agriculture, Dalhousie University">Faculty of Agriculture</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Bible_Hill,_Nova_Scotia" title="Bible Hill, Nova Scotia">Bible Hill</a>, Nova Scotia.<sup id="cite_ref-Dal_name_hailed_in_Bible_Hill_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dal_name_hailed_in_Bible_Hill-23"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Dalhousie operates three campuses within the <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Peninsula" title="Halifax Peninsula">Halifax Peninsula</a>, and one located in Bible Hill, Nova Scotia. The largest, Studley Campus, serves as the primary campus; it houses the majority of the university's academic buildings such as faculties, athletic facilities, and the university's Student Union Building.<sup id="cite_ref-camp_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camp-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The campus is largely surrounded by residential neighbourhoods. <a href="/wiki/Robie_Street" title="Robie Street">Robie Street</a> divides it from adjacent Carleton Campus, which houses the faculties of dentistry, medicine, and other health profession departments. The campus is adjacent to two large teaching hospitals affiliated with the school: the <a href="/wiki/IWK_Health_Centre" title="IWK Health Centre">IWK Health Centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II_Health_Sciences_Centre" title="Queen Elizabeth II Health Sciences Centre">Queen Elizabeth II Health Sciences Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-camp_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camp-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Sexton Campus is within the core of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Halifax" title="Downtown Halifax">Downtown Halifax</a>; it hosts the engineering, architecture and planning faculties. Sexton Campus served as the campus of the Technical University of Nova Scotia prior to amalgamation.<sup id="cite_ref-camp_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camp-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The Agricultural Campus in Bible Hill, a suburban community of <a href="/wiki/Truro,_Nova_Scotia" title="Truro, Nova Scotia">Truro</a>, Nova Scotia, served as the campus for the Nova Scotia Agricultural College prior to its merger with Dalhousie in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The buildings at Dalhousie vary in age, from Hart House which was completed in 1864, to the Mona Campbell Building which was completed in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The original building of Dalhousie University was completed in 1824 in Halifax's <a href="/wiki/Grand_Parade_(Halifax)" title="Grand Parade (Halifax)">Grand Parade</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-orib_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orib-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> it was demolished in 1885 when the university required a larger one, and the City of Halifax sought possession of the entire Grand Parade. <a href="/wiki/Halifax_City_Hall" title="Halifax City Hall">Halifax City Hall</a> presently occupies the space of the original Dalhousie building.<sup id="cite_ref-orib_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orib-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_museums">Libraries and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Libraries and museums">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university has five libraries. The largest, <a href="/wiki/Killam_Library" title="Killam Library">Killam Memorial Library</a>, opened in 1971. It is the largest academic library in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a> with over one million books and 40,000 journals. The library's collection largely serves the faculties of arts and social sciences, sciences, management, and computer science.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The W. K. Kellogg Health Science Library provides services largely for the faculties of dentistry, medicine, and other health professions.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The Sexton Design &amp; Technology Library is located within Sexton Campus. Its collection largely serves those in the faculties of engineering, architecture and planning, and houses the university's rare books collection.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The Sir James Dunn Law Library holds the university's collection of common law materials, legal periodicals, as well as books on international law, health law, and environmental law.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> MacRae Library is located at the university's Agricultural Campus, and has the largest collection of agricultural resource material in Atlantic Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The Dalhousie University Archives houses official records of, or relating to, or people/activities connected with Dalhousie University and its founding institutions. The archives also houses material related to theatre, business and labour in Nova Scotia. The collection consists of manuscripts, texts, photographs, audio-visual material, microfilm, music, and artifacts. <sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The biology department operates the Thomas McCulloch Museum. The most notable of the museum's exhibits is its preserved birds collection. Other exhibits include its collection of lorenzen ceramic mushrooms, its coral and shell collection, and its butterfly and insect collection.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> The museum's namesake <a href="/wiki/Thomas_McCulloch" title="Thomas McCulloch">Thomas McCulloch</a> was a Scottish Presbyterian minister who served as Dalhousie's first president and created the Audubon mounted bird collection which is now housed at the museum.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Dalhousie Art Gallery is both a public gallery and an academic support unit housed since 1971 on the lowest level of the <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Arts_Centre" title="Dalhousie Arts Centre">Dalhousie Arts Centre</a>. Admission is free of charge. It is host to a permanent collection of over 1000 works.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Some of the outdoor sculptures around the campus are part of this collection, such as the distinctive <i>Marine Venus</i> which has sat in the median of University Avenue since it was exhibited at <a href="/wiki/Expo_67" title="Expo 67">Expo 67</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing_and_student_facilities">Housing and student facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Housing and student facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university has ten student residences throughout its Halifax campuses: Eliza Ritchie Hall, Gerard Hall, Howe Hall, Mini Rez, O'Brien Hall, Residence Houses, Risley Hall, Shirreff Hall, Glengary Apartments, and Graduate House.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest, Howe Hall in Studley Campus, houses 716 students during the academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also operates three residences in its Agricultural Campus: Chapman House, Fraser House, and Truman House. The largest residence in the Agricultural Campus is Chapman House, housing 125 students during the academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The residences are represented by a Residence Council responsible for resident concerns, providing entertainment services, organizing events, and upholding rules and regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Student Union Building serves as the main <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student activity centre</a>. Completed in 1968, it is located in the Studley Campus. The Student Union building hosts a number of student societies and organization offices, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Student_Union" title="Dalhousie Student Union">Dalhousie Student Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-camp_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-camp-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The building houses five restaurants, both independently owned and international franchises such as <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hortons" title="Tim Hortons">Tim Hortons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Office of Sustainability, created in 2008, is charged with creating campus solutions that support positive ecological, social health, and economic outcomes.<sup id="cite_ref-sust_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sust-45"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> These efforts largely focus on policy and planning; communication and learning; and project development and management.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is party to a number of environmental treaties. In 1999, the university signed the <a href="/wiki/Talloires_Declaration" title="Talloires Declaration">Talloires Declaration</a>, which committed Dalhousie and other higher education institutions to developing, creating, supporting, and maintaining sustainability.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, the university signed the <i>University and College Presidents’ Climate Change Statement of Action for Canada</i> to reduce emissions of greenhouse gases.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie is a signatory of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environmental_Programme" title="United Nations Environmental Programme" class="mw-redirect">UNEP</a>'s International Declaration on Cleaner Production.<sup id="cite_ref-sust_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sust-45"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several programs from the university placed in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Knights" title="Corporate Knights">Corporate Knights</a> rankings, which measures how well Canadian universities integrate sustainability into their curriculum. Dalhousie's School of Business Administration ranked seventh in Canada for undergraduate business programs. The Corporate Knights ranked the business school tenth in Canada for its MBA program. The Faculty of Law ranked third in Canada for law.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The university campus received a B grade from the Sustainable Endowments Institute on its College Sustainability Report Card for 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Henry-hicks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Henry Hicks Academic Administration Building at Dalhousie University" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Henry-hicks.jpg/220px-Henry-hicks.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Henry-hicks.jpg/330px-Henry-hicks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Henry-hicks.jpg/440px-Henry-hicks.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Henry-hicks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Henry Hicks Academic Administration Building is located at Dalhousie's Studley Campus, and houses many of Dalhousie's administrative offices.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>University governance is conducted through the Board of Governors and the Senate, both of which were given much of their present powers in the Unofficial Consolidation of an Act for the Regulation and Support of Dalhousie College in Chapter 24 of the Acts of 1863. This statute replaced ones from 1820, 1823, 1838, 1841 and 1848, and has since been supplemented 11 times, the latest in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-dalsta_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalsta-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board is responsible for conduct, management, and control of the university and of its property, revenues, business, and affairs. Board members, known as Governors of the Board, include the university's chancellor, president, and 25 other members. Members include people from within the university community such as four approved representatives from Dalhousie Student Union, and those in the surrounding community, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Halifax" title="Mayor of Halifax" class="mw-redirect">Mayor of Halifax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dalsta_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalsta-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate is responsible for the university's academics, including standards for admission and qualifications for degrees, diplomas, and certificates.<sup id="cite_ref-dalsta_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dalsta-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The Senate consists of 73 positions granted to the various faculty representatives, academic administrators, and student representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The president acts as the chief executive officer and is responsible to the Board of Governors and to the Senate for the supervision of administrative and academic works. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richard_Florizone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Richard Florizone (page does not exist)">Richard Florizone</a> is the 11th president of the university, and has served since 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Thomas McCulloch served as the first president when the office was created in 1838. <a href="/wiki/John_Forrest_(Canadian_clergyman)" title="John Forrest (Canadian clergyman)">John Forrest</a> was the longest-serving president, holding the office from 1885 to 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Affiliated_institutions">Affiliated institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Affiliated institutions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_King%27s_College" title="University of King's College">University of King's College</a> is a post-secondary institution in Halifax affiliated with Dalhousie. Established in 1789, it was the first post-secondary institution in <a href="/wiki/English_Canada" title="English Canada">English Canada</a> and the oldest English-speaking Commonwealth university outside the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-kinhi_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kinhi-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of King's College was originally an independent institution located in <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Nova_Scotia" title="Windsor, Nova Scotia">Windsor</a>, Nova Scotia, until 1920, when a fire ravaged its campus. To continue operation, the University of King's College accepted a generous grant from the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Corporation_of_New_York" title="Carnegie Corporation of New York">Carnegie Foundation</a>, although the terms of the grant required that it move to Halifax and enter into association with Dalhousie.<sup id="cite_ref-kinhi_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kinhi-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Under the agreement, King's agreed to pay the salaries of a number of Dalhousie professors, who in turn were to help in the management and academic life of the College. Students at King's were to have access to all of the amenities Dalhousie, and the academic programs at King's would fold into the College of Arts and Sciences at Dalhousie.<sup id="cite_ref-kinhi_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kinhi-54"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Presently, students of both institutions are allowed to switch between the two throughout their enrolment. In spite of the shared academic programs and facilities, the University of King's College maintains its own scholarships, bursaries, athletics programs, and student residences.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university completed the 2011–12 year with revenues of $573.597 million and expenses of $536.451 million, yielding a surplus of $37.146 million.<sup id="cite_ref-finrep_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finrep-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest source of revenue for the university was provincial operational grants, which made up 32 percent of revenue. Tuition fees generated $123.2 million in the 2011–12 fiscal year, making up 21 percent of revenue. As of 31&nbsp;March&nbsp;2012<span style="display:none">&nbsp;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2012-03-31</span>)</span><sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Dalhousie's endowment was valued at $400.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-finrep_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finrep-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Dalhousie is a publicly funded research university, and a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a>, a group of Canadian research-intensive universities.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 18,220 students enrolled at the university and 3,700 courses in over 190 degree programs.<sup id="cite_ref-qfacts_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qfacts-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alum_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alum-58"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie offers more than 3,700 courses and 190 degree programs in twelve undergraduate, graduate, and professional faculties.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The requirements for admission differ between students from Nova Scotia, students from other provinces in Canada, and international students due to lack of uniformity in marking schemes. The requirements for admission also differ depending on the program. In 2011, the secondary school average for incoming first-year undergraduate students was 85 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-qfacts_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qfacts-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Canadian students may apply for financial aid such as the Nova Scotia Student Assistance Program and <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_Canada" title="Student loans in Canada">Canada Student Loans and Grants</a> through the federal and provincial governments. Financial aid may also be provided in the form of loans, grants, bursaries, scholarships, fellowships, debt reduction, interest relief, and work programs.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation">Reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Reputation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="infobox" cellspacing="3" style="border-spacing:3px;width:22em;width:23em; font-size:75%;">

          <ul> 
           <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Canadian_university_rankings" title="Template:Canadian university rankings"><span title="View this template" style="">v</span></a></li>

     <p>Dalhousie has consistently been ranked one of Canada's top universities. The 2012–2013 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a> placed Dalhousie 251–275th in the world, the seventeenth highest in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> ranked the university 234th.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> rankings, the university ranked 201–300 in the world and 8–17th in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN-62"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of national rankings, <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> ranked Dalhousie tied for 7th in their 2013 Medical Doctoral university rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-63"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie was ranked in spite of having opted out—along with several other universities in Canada—of participating in Maclean's graduate survey since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A number of Dalhousie's individual programs and faculties have gained accolades nationally and internationally. In Maclean's 2012 <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> school rankings, the Schulich School of Law placed 6th in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In the QS rankings of law programs, the university placed 51–100 in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie had also placed in ARWU's rankings for the field of social sciences at 151–200th.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC-61"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The Faculty of Management was named the most innovative business school in Canada by European CEO magazine on 17 November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Dalhousie University is a member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a>, a group that represents 15 of Canada’s most research-intensive universities. Out of 50 universities in Canada, Research Infosource ranked Dalhousie University the 16th most research-intensive for 2011, with a sponsored research income of $125.147 million, averaging $124,500 per faculty member.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003 and 2004, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scientist" title="The Scientist">The Scientist</a></i> placed Dalhousie among the top five places in the world outside the United States for postdoctoral work and conducting scientific research.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007 Dalhousie topped the list of <i>The Scientist</i>’s “Best Places to Work in Academia”. The annual list divides research and academic institutions into American and international lists; Dalhousie University ranked first in the international category.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> According to a survey conducted by <i>The Scientist</i>, Dalhousie was the best non-commercial scientific institute in which to work in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In terms of research performance, <a href="/wiki/High_Impact_Universities" title="High Impact Universities">High Impact Universities</a> 2010 ranked Dalhousie 239th out of 500 universities, and 12th in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was ranked 194th out of 500 universities and 12th in the country for research performance in the fields of medicine, dentistry, pharmacology, and health sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT) ranked Dalhousie 279th in the world and 12th in Canada for its 2011 <a href="/wiki/Performance_Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers_for_World_Universities" title="Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities">scientific paper's performances</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> HEEACT had also ranked Dalhousie 86th in the world and fourth nationally for research performance in <a href="/wiki/Earth_science" title="Earth science">geoscience</a> in its 2010 rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Marine research at Dalhousie has become a large focus of the university, with many of the university's faculty members involved in some form of marine research.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Notably, Dalhousie is the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Tracking_Network" title="Ocean Tracking Network">Ocean Tracking Network</a>, a research effort using implanted acoustic transmitters to study fish migration patterns.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie houses a number of marine research pools, a <a href="/wiki/Wet_laboratory" title="Wet laboratory">wet laboratory</a>, and a benthic flume, which are collectively known as the Aquatron laboratory.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie is one of the founding members of the Halifax Marine Research Institute, founded on 2 June 2011. The institute, which is a partnership between a number of private industries, government, and post-secondary institutions, was designed to help increase the scale, quality, internationalization and impact of marine research in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the university, along with <a href="/wiki/WWF-Canada" title="WWF-Canada">WWF-Canada</a>, created the Conservation Legacy For Oceans, which aimed at providing scholarships, funding, curriculum development, and work placements for students and academics dedicated to marine research, law, management, and policy making.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many of Dalhousie's faculties and departments focus on marine research. The Faculty of Engineering operates the Ocean Research Centre Atlantic, which is dedicated to research and tests in naval and off-shore engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Schulich School of Law also operates the Marine &amp; Environmental Law Institute, which carries out research and conducts consultancy activities for governmental and non-governmental organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The school's Department of Political Science similarly operates the Centre for Foreign Policy Studies, which is primarily concerned with the fields of Canadian and American foreign, security, and defence policy, including maritime security policy.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The student body of Dalhousie is currently represented by two <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">students' unions</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Student_Union" title="Dalhousie Student Union">Dalhousie Student Union</a>, which represents the general student population, and the Dalhousie Association for Graduate Students, which represents the interests of graduate students specifically.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie Student Union began as the Dalhousie Student Government in 1863, and was renamed the University Student Council before taking its present name.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> The student union recognizes more than 100 student organizations and societies.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The organizations and clubs accredited at Queen's cover a wide range of interests including academics, culture, religion, social issues, and recreation. Accredited extracurricular organizations at the university fall under the jurisdiction of the Dalhousie Student Union, and must conform to its by-laws.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2011, there were three sororities (Omega Pi, Iota Beta Chi, and Pi Gamma Delta) and three fraternities (<a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, and Phi Kappa Pi).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> They operate as non-accredited organizations and are not recognized by the Dalhousie Student Union.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's student population operates a number of media outlets. The university's main <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student newspaper</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dalhousie_Gazette" title="The Dalhousie Gazette">The Dalhousie Gazette</a></i>, claims to be the oldest student-run newspaper in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-DalGz_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DalGz-91"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> It is published Fridays, and is distributed to 200 locations around the Halifax area. The newspaper's offices are in the Student Union building.<sup id="cite_ref-DalGz_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DalGz-91"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie's student population runs a radio station which began as a radio club in 1964, and began to broadcast and operate as <a href="/wiki/CKDU" title="CKDU" class="mw-redirect">CKDU</a> in 1975; it began <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">FM frequency</a> broadcasting in 1985. CKDU changed to its present frequency 88.1 in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Dalhousie's sports teams are called the Tigers. The Tigers varsity teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_University_Sport" title="Atlantic University Sport">Atlantic University Sport</a> (AUS) of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a> (CIS). Teams include basketball, hockey, soccer, swimming, track and field, cross country running, and volleyball. The Tigers garnered a number of championships in the first decade of the 20th century, winning 63 AUS championships and 2 CIS championships.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> More than 2,500 students participate in competitive clubs, intramural sport leagues, and tournaments. Opportunities are offered at multiple skill levels across a variety of sports. Dalhousie has 6 competitive sports clubs and 17 recreational clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Dalhousie's Agricultural Campus operates its own varsity team, called the Dalhousie Rams. The Rams varsity team participates in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="Atlantic Collegiate Athletic Association">Atlantic Collegiate Athletic Association</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="Canadian Collegiate Athletic Association">Canadian Collegiate Athletic Association</a>. The Rams varsity teams include badminton, basketball, rugby, soccer, volleyball, and <a href="/wiki/Woodsman" title="Woodsman">woodsmen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Dalhousie has a number of athletic facilities open to varsity teams and students. Dalplex is the largest main fitness and recreational facility.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The stadium with the largest seating capacity is Wickwire Field, with a seating capacity of up to 1,200. Wickwire Field is the university's main outdoor facilities and is host to the varsity football, soccer, field hockey, lacrosse and rugby teams.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Other sporting facilities include Memorial Arena, home to the varsity hockey teams, Studley Gymnasium, the Sexton Gymnasium and field.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> The Agricultural Campus has one athletic facility, the Langille Athletic Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Insignia_and_other_representations">Insignia and other representations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Insignia and other representations">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seal">Seal</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Seal">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Dalhousie seal is based on the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">heraldic achievement</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Clan_Ramsay" title="Clan Ramsay">Clan Ramsay</a> of Scotland, of which founder George Ramsay was clan head. The heraldic achievement consists of five parts: shield, coronet, crest, supporters, and motto. One major difference between the Ramsay coat of arms and the university seal is that the Ramsay seal features a <a href="/wiki/Griffin" title="Griffin">griffin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greyhound" title="Greyhound">greyhound</a>, and the Dalhousie seal has two dragons supporting the eagle-adorned shield.<sup id="cite_ref-seal_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seal-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Initially, the Ramsay coat of arms was used to identify Dalhousie, but the seal has evolved with the amalgamations the university has undergone.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The seal was originally silver-coloured, but in 1950, the university's Board of Governors changed it to gold to match the university's colours, gold and black. These colurs were adopted in 1887, after the rugby team led the debate about college colours for football jerseys.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite1997128_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite1997128-103"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The shield and eagle of Dalhousie's seal have been used as the logo since 1987, with the present incarnation in use since 2003, which includes the tagline &quot;inspiring minds&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-seal_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seal-101"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motto_and_song">Motto and song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Motto and song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university motto <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Ora et Labora</i></span> translates from Latin as &quot;pray and work&quot;; it adopted in 1870 from the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Dalhousie" title="Earl of Dalhousie">Earl of Dalhousie</a>'s motto to replace the university's original one, which the administration believed did not convey confidence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite199798_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite199798-104"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The original motto was <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Forsan</i></span>, which tranlsates as <i>Perhaps</i>, and first appeared in the first <i>Dalhousie Gazette</i> of 1869. It was from <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">epic poem</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Aeneid" title="Aeneid">Aeneid</a></i>, Book&nbsp;1, line 203, <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Forsan et haec olim meminisse iuvabit</i></span>, which translates as &quot;Perhaps the time may come when these difficulties will be sweet to remember&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWaite1997128_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWaite1997128-103"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A number of songs are commonly played and sung at various events such as commencement, convocation, and athletic contests, including &quot;Carmina Dalhousiana&quot;, written in Halifax in 1882. The Dalhousie University songbook was compiled by Charles B. Weikel in 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2>

     <div class="rellink">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Dalhousie_University_people" title="List of Dalhousie University people">List of Dalhousie University people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Dalhousie graduates have found success in a variety of fields, serving as the heads of diverse public and private institutions. Dalhousie University has over 110,000 alumni. Throughout Dalhousie's history, faculty, alumni, and former students have played prominent roles in many fields, and include 87 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notable politicians who have graduated from Dalhousie include two <a href="/wiki/Prime_Ministers_of_Canada" title="Prime Ministers of Canada" class="mw-redirect">Prime Ministers of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/R._B._Bennett" title="R. B. Bennett">R.&nbsp;B. Bennett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Clark" title="Joe Clark">Joe Clark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Canadian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Brian_Mulroney" title="Brian Mulroney">Brian Mulroney</a> attended <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Law_School" title="Dalhousie Law School" class="mw-redirect">Dalhousie Law School</a>, though he failed after his first year.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Eight graduates have served as <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(Canada)" title="Lieutenant governor (Canada)">Lieutenant Governors</a>: <a href="/wiki/John_Crosbie" title="John Crosbie">John Crosbie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Myra_Freeman" title="Myra Freeman">Myra Freeman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NovPre_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NovPre-111"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Gosse" title="Clarence Gosse">Clarence Gosse</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Keiller_MacKay" title="John Keiller MacKay">John Keiller MacKay</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Henry_Poole_MacKeen" title="Henry Poole MacKeen">Henry Poole MacKeen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NovPre_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NovPre-111"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Robert_Nicholson" title="John Robert Nicholson">John Robert Nicholson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fabian_O%27Dea" title="Fabian O'Dea">Fabian O'Dea</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Walsh" title="Albert Walsh">Albert Walsh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Twelve graduates have served as provincial <a href="/wiki/Premier_(Canada)" title="Premier (Canada)">premiers</a>: <a href="/wiki/Allan_Blakeney" title="Allan Blakeney">Allan Blakeney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Buchanan" title="John Buchanan">John Buchanan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alex_Campbell_(politician)" title="Alex Campbell (politician)">Alex Campbell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amor_De_Cosmos" title="Amor De Cosmos">Amor De Cosmos</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Dexter" title="Darrell Dexter">Darrell Dexter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ghiz" title="Joe Ghiz">Joe Ghiz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Hamm" title="John Hamm">John Hamm</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Angus_Lewis_Macdonald" title="Angus Lewis Macdonald">Angus Lewis Macdonald</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russell_MacLellan" title="Russell MacLellan">Russell MacLellan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Regan" title="Gerald Regan">Gerald Regan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gerald_Regan.27s_.27amazing.27_victory_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerald_Regan.27s_.27amazing.27_victory-127"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stanfield" title="Robert Stanfield">Robert Stanfield</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Gerald_Regan.27s_.27amazing.27_victory_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gerald_Regan.27s_.27amazing.27_victory-127"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Wells" title="Clyde Wells">Clyde Wells</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Williams_(politician)" title="Danny Williams (politician)">Danny Williams</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> The first woman appointed to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bertha_Wilson" title="Bertha Wilson">Bertha Wilson</a>, was a graduate from Dalhousie Law School.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Prominent business leaders who studied at Dalhousie include <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Baillie" title="Jamie Baillie">Jamie Baillie</a>, former CEO of Credit Union Atlantic,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Graham_Day" title="Graham Day">Graham Day</a>, former CEO of <a href="/wiki/British_Shipbuilders" title="British Shipbuilders">British Shipbuilders</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sean_Durfy" title="Sean Durfy">Sean Durfy</a>, former CEO of <a href="/wiki/WestJet" title="WestJet">WestJet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Peter_McColough" title="Charles Peter McColough">Charles Peter McColough</a>, former president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> Other notable graduates of Dalhousie includes <a href="/wiki/Donald_O._Hebb" title="Donald O. Hebb">Donald O. Hebb</a>, who helped advanced the field of <a href="/wiki/Neuropsychology" title="Neuropsychology">neuropsychology</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_D._Sullivan" title="Kathryn D. Sullivan">Kathryn D. Sullivan</a>, the first American woman to walk in space.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Dalhousie_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: References">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">

      <li><span id="CITEREFWaite1997" class="citation book">Waite, P. (1997). <i>Lives of Dalhousie University: 1925–1980, The Old College Transformed</i>. McGill-Queen's Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-7735-1644-1" title="Special:BookSources/0-7735-1644-1">0-7735-1644-1</a>.</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADalhousie+University&amp;rft.aufirst=P.&amp;rft.aulast=Waite&amp;rft.au=Waite%2C+P.&amp;rft.btitle=Lives+of+Dalhousie+University%3A+1925%E2%80%931980%2C+The+Old+College+Transformed&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=0-7735-1644-1&amp;rft.pub=McGill-Queen%27s+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></li>
